<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Colonialism</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Creation and maintenance of colonies by people from another area</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Musee-de-lArmee-IMG_0976.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2500" data-file-width="2500" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Musee-de-lArmee-IMG_0976.jpg/220px-Musee-de-lArmee-IMG_0976.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Musee-de-lArmee-IMG_0976.jpg/330px-Musee-de-lArmee-IMG_0976.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Musee-de-lArmee-IMG_0976.jpg/440px-Musee-de-lArmee-IMG_0976.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Musee-de-lArmee-IMG_0976.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Pith_helmet" title="Pith helmet">pith helmet</a>, an icon of colonialism in tropical lands. This one was used by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Madagascar" title="Kingdom of Madagascar">Kingdom of Madagascar</a>, inspired by those used by the <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire#Second_French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">Second French colonial empire</a>.</div></div></div>
<p><b>Colonialism</b> is a practice or policy of control by one people or power over other people or areas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stanford_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stanford-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Collins_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Collins-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Webster_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Webster-3">[3]</a></sup> often by establishing <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colonies</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oster_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oster-4">[4]</a></sup> and generally with the aim of economic dominance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> In the process of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonisation" title="Colonisation">colonisation</a>, colonisers may impose their religion, language, economics, and other cultural practices. The foreign administrators rule the territory in pursuit of their interests, seeking to benefit from the colonised region's people and resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> It is associated with but distinct from <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">imperialism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stanford_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stanford-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>Though colonialism <a href="/wiki/Colonies_in_antiquity" title="Colonies in antiquity">has existed since ancient times</a>, the concept is most strongly associated with the <a href="/wiki/History_of_colonialism" title="History of colonialism">European colonial period</a> starting with the 15th century when some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_colonial_empires" title="European colonial empires">European states established colonising empires</a>.
</p><p>At first, European colonising countries followed policies of <a href="/wiki/Mercantilism" title="Mercantilism">mercantilism</a>, aiming to strengthen the home-country economy, so agreements usually restricted the colony to trading only with the <a href="/wiki/Metropole" title="Metropole">metropole</a> (mother country). By the mid-19th century, the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> gave up mercantilism and trade restrictions and adopted the principle of <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a>, with few restrictions or <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariffs</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Christian_mission" title="Christian mission">Christian missionaries</a> were active in practically all of the European-controlled colonies because the <a href="/wiki/Metropole" title="Metropole">metropoles</a> were Christian.
</p><p>Historian Philip Hoffman calculated that by 1800, before the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Europeans" title="Europeans">Europeans</a> already controlled at least 35% of the globe, and by 1914, they had gained control of 84% of the globe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_II" title="Aftermath of World War II">aftermath of World War II</a> colonial powers retreated between 1945 and 1975; over which time nearly all colonies gained <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a>, entering into changed colonial, so-called <a href="/wiki/Postcolonialism" title="Postcolonialism">postcolonial</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neocolonialism" title="Neocolonialism">neocolonialist</a> relations.
</p><p>Postcolonialism and neocolonialism have continued or shifted relations and ideologies of colonialism, justifying its continuation with concepts such as <a href="/wiki/Development_aid" title="Development aid">development</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Frontier" title="New Frontier">new frontiers</a>, as in exploring <a href="/wiki/Space_colonization" title="Space colonization">outer space for colonization</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fundacion_de_Santiago.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="944" data-file-width="1330" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Fundacion_de_Santiago.jpg/220px-Fundacion_de_Santiago.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Fundacion_de_Santiago.jpg/330px-Fundacion_de_Santiago.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Fundacion_de_Santiago.jpg/440px-Fundacion_de_Santiago.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fundacion_de_Santiago.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1541: Spanish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conquistadors" title="Conquistadors">Conquistadors</a> founding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Chile" title="Santiago de Chile">Santiago de Chile</a></div></div></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Collins_English_Dictionary" title="Collins English Dictionary">Collins English Dictionary</a></i> defines colonialism as "the practice by which a powerful country directly controls less powerful countries and uses their resources to increase its own power and wealth".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Collins_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Collins-2">[2]</a></sup> <i>Webster's Encyclopedic Dictionary</i> defines colonialism as "the system or policy of a nation seeking to extend or retain its authority over other people or territories".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Webster_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Webster-3">[3]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Merriam-Webster" title="Merriam-Webster">Merriam-Webster</a> Dictionary</i> offers four definitions, including "something characteristic of a colony" and "control by one power over a dependent area or people".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Etymologically, the word "<a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/colony" title="wikt:colony">colony</a>" comes from the Latin <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/col%C5%8Dnia" title="wikt:colōnia">colōnia</a></i>—"a place for agriculture".
</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Stanford_Encyclopedia_of_Philosophy" title="Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy">Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy</a></i> uses the term "to describe the process of European settlement and political control over the rest of the world, including the Americas, Australia, and parts of Africa and Asia". It discusses the distinction between colonialism, <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">imperialism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conquest" title="Conquest">conquest</a> and states that "[t]he difficulty of defining colonialism stems from the fact that the term is often used as a synonym for imperialism. Both colonialism and imperialism were forms of conquest that were expected to benefit Europe economically and strategically," and continues "given the difficulty of consistently distinguishing between the two terms, this entry will use <i>colonialism</i> broadly to refer to the project of European political domination from the sixteenth to the twentieth centuries that ended with the national liberation movements of the 1960s".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stanford_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-Stanford-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>In his preface to <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Osterhammel" title="Jürgen Osterhammel">Jürgen Osterhammel</a>'s <i>Colonialism: A Theoretical Overview</i>, Roger Tignor says "For Osterhammel, the essence of colonialism is the existence of colonies, which are by definition governed differently from other territories such as protectorates or informal spheres of influence."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oster_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Oster-4">[4]</a></sup> In the book, Osterhammel asks, "How can 'colonialism' be defined independently from 'colony?'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> He settles on a three-sentence definition:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Colonialism is a relationship between an indigenous (or forcibly imported) majority and a minority of foreign invaders. The fundamental decisions affecting the lives of the colonised people are made and implemented by the colonial rulers in pursuit of interests that are often defined in a distant metropolis. Rejecting cultural compromises with the colonised population, the colonisers are convinced of their own superiority and their ordained mandate to rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types">Types</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rijsttafel_TMnr_60053682.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="674" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rijsttafel_TMnr_60053682.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rijsttafel_TMnr_60053682.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rijsttafel_TMnr_60053682.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rijsttafel_TMnr_60053682.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rijsttafel_TMnr_60053682.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rijsttafel_TMnr_60053682.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rijsttafel_TMnr_60053682.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dutch family in <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>, 1927</div></div></div>
<p><i>The Times</i> once quipped that there were three types of colonial empire: "The English, which consists in making colonies with colonists; the German, which collects colonists without colonies; the French, which sets up colonies without colonists."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Modern studies of colonialism have often distinguished between various overlapping categories of colonialism, broadly classified into four types: <a href="/wiki/Settler_colonialism" title="Settler colonialism">settler colonialism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exploitation_colonialism" title="Exploitation colonialism">exploitation colonialism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surrogate_Colonialism" title="Surrogate Colonialism">surrogate colonialism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Internal_colonialism" title="Internal colonialism">internal colonialism</a>. Some historians have identified other forms of colonialism, including national and trade forms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Settler colonialism involves large-scale <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a> by <a href="/wiki/Settler" title="Settler">settlers</a> to colonies, often motivated by religious, political, or economic reasons. This form of colonialism aims largely to supplant prior existing populations with a settler one, and involves large number of settlers emigrating to colonies for the purpose of settling down and establishing settlements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> (and to a more controversial extent <a href="/wiki/Israel_and_apartheid" title="Israel and apartheid">Israel</a>) are examples of nations created in their modern form by settler colonization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></li>
<li>Exploitation colonialism involves fewer colonists and focuses on the exploitation of natural resources or labour to the benefit of the <a href="/wiki/Metropole" title="Metropole">metropole</a>. This form consists of <a href="/wiki/Trading_post" title="Trading post">trading posts</a> as well as larger colonies where colonists would constitute much of the political and economic administration. The European <a href="/wiki/Colonisation_of_Africa" title="Colonisation of Africa">colonization of Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_imperialism_in_Asia" title="Western imperialism in Asia">Asia</a> was largely conducted under the auspices of exploitation colonialism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></li>
<li>Surrogate colonialism involves a settlement project supported by a colonial power, in which most of the settlers do not come from the same ethnic group as the ruling power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></li>
<li>Internal colonialism is a notion of uneven structural power between areas of a <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a>. The source of exploitation comes from within the state. This is demonstrated in the way control and exploitation may pass from people from the colonizing country to an immigrant population within a newly independent country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></li>
<li>National colonialism is a process involving elements of both settler and internal colonialism, in which nation-building and colonization are symbiotically connected, with the colonial regime seeking to remake the colonized peoples into their own cultural and political image. The goal is to integrate them into the state, but only as reflections of the state's preferred culture. <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">The Republic of China in Taiwan</a> is the archetypal example of a national-colonialist society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></li>
<li>Trade colonialism involves the undertaking of colonialist ventures in support of trade opportunities for merchants. This form of colonialism was most prominent in 19th-century Asia, where previously <a href="/wiki/Isolationism" title="Isolationism">isolationist</a> states were forced to open their ports to Western powers. Examples of this include the <a href="/wiki/Opium_Wars" title="Opium Wars">Opium Wars</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bakumatsu" title="Bakumatsu">opening of Japan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Socio-cultural_evolution">Socio-cultural evolution</span></h2>
<p>As colonialism often played out in pre-populated areas, <a href="/wiki/Sociocultural_evolution" title="Sociocultural evolution">sociocultural evolution</a> included the formation of various ethnically hybrid populations. Colonialism gave rise to culturally and ethnically mixed populations such as the <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizos</a> of the Americas, as well as racially divided populations such as those found in <a href="/wiki/French_Algeria" title="French Algeria">French Algeria</a> or in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rhodesia" title="Southern Rhodesia">Southern Rhodesia</a>. In fact, everywhere where colonial powers established a consistent and continued presence, hybrid communities existed.
</p><p>Notable examples in Asia include the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Burmese_people" title="Anglo-Burmese people">Anglo-Burmese</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Indian" title="Anglo-Indian">Anglo-Indian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burgher_people" title="Burgher people">Burgher</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurasian_Singaporean" title="Eurasian Singaporean">Eurasian Singaporean</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filipino_mestizo" title="Filipino mestizo">Filipino mestizo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kristang_people" title="Kristang people">Kristang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macanese_people" title="Macanese people">Macanese peoples</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> (later <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>) the vast majority of "Dutch" settlers were in fact Eurasians known as <a href="/wiki/Indo_people" title="Indo people">Indo-Europeans</a>, formally belonging to the European legal class in the colony (see also <a href="/wiki/Indos_in_pre-colonial_history" title="Indos in pre-colonial history">Indos in pre-colonial history</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indos_in_colonial_history" title="Indos in colonial history">Indos in colonial history</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1062260506">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:.5em 1.4em .8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{overflow:hidden;position:relative;margin:.5em auto .8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft span,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright span{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox>blockquote{margin:0;padding:0;border-left:0;font-family:inherit;font-size:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote>:first-child{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote:last-child>:last-child{margin-bottom:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quote-title,.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quotebox-quote{display:block}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 .8em!important;float:none!important}}</style><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:25%; ;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p>"Why do the Christian nations, which were so weak in the past compared with Muslim nations begin to dominate so many lands in modern times and even defeat the once victorious Ottoman armies?"..."Because they have laws and rules invented by reason."
</p>
</blockquote>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style=""><a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Muteferrika" title="Ibrahim Muteferrika">Ibrahim Muteferrika</a>, <i>Rational basis for the Politics of Nations</i> (1731)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiquity">Antiquity</span></h3>
<p>Activity that could be called colonialism has a long history, starting at least as early as the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Ancient Egyptians</a>. <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicians</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_colonization" title="Greek colonization">Greeks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a> founded <a href="/wiki/Colonies_in_antiquity" title="Colonies in antiquity">colonies in antiquity</a>. <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicia</a> had an enterprising maritime trading-culture that spread across the Mediterranean from 1550 BC to 300 BC; later the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persian_empire" title="Persian empire">Persian empire</a> and various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_colonization" title="Greek colonization">Greek city-states</a> continued on this line of setting up colonies. The <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a> would soon follow, setting up <a href="/wiki/Colonia_(Roman)" title="Colonia (Roman)"><i>coloniae</i></a> throughout the Mediterranean, in Northern Africa, and in Western Asia. Beginning in the 7th century, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_Empire" title="Arab Empire">Arabs</a> colonized a substantial portion of the Middle East, Northern Africa, and parts of Asia and Europe. From the 9th century <a href="/wiki/Viking_Age" title="Viking Age">Vikings</a> (<a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norsemen</a>) established <a href="/wiki/Viking_expansion" title="Viking expansion">colonies</a> in Britain, Ireland, Iceland, Greenland, North America, present-day Russia and Ukraine, France (Normandy) and Sicily. In the 9th century a new wave of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a> colonisation began, with competitors such as the <a href="/wiki/Stato_da_M%C3%A0r" title="Stato da Màr">Venetians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genoese_colonies" title="Genoese colonies">Genovese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Amalfi" title="Duchy of Amalfi">Amalfians</a> infiltrating the wealthy previously <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine" title="Byzantine">Byzantine</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman" title="Eastern Roman">Eastern Roman</a> islands and lands. European <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crusaders" title="Crusaders">Crusaders</a> set up colonial regimes in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outremer" title="Outremer">Outremer</a> (in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Levant" title="The Levant">the Levant</a>, 1097–1291) and in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic littoral</a> (12th century onwards). <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venice</a> began to dominate <a href="/wiki/Dalmatia" title="Dalmatia">Dalmatia</a> and reached its greatest nominal colonial extent at the conclusion of the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Crusade" title="Fourth Crusade">Fourth Crusade</a> in 1204, with the declaration of the <a href="/wiki/Partitio_terrarum_imperii_Romaniae" title="Partitio terrarum imperii Romaniae">acquisition of three octaves</a> of the Byzantine Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modernity">Modernity</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1303" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png/300px-Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png/450px-Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png/600px-Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a> of Spain and Portugal between 1580 and 1640</div></div></div>
<p>More than a century before the <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">Jamestown, Virginia</a> settlement led by captain <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Newport" title="Christopher Newport">Christopher Newport</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> modern colonialism started with the Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Prince_Henry_the_Navigator" title="Prince Henry the Navigator">Prince Henry the Navigator</a> (1394–1460), initiating the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Age_of_Exploration" title="Age of Exploration">Age of Exploration</a> and establishing African trading posts (1445 onwards). Spain (initially the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a>) and soon after Portugal encountered the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> (1492 onwards) through sea travel and built trading posts or conquered large extents of land. For some people,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (February 2021)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup> it is this building of colonies across oceans that differentiates colonialism from other types of <a href="/wiki/Expansionism" title="Expansionism">expansionism</a>. Madrid and Lisbon <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">divided the areas of these "new" lands</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> in 1494; other would-be colonial powers paid little heed to the theoretical demarcation.
</p><p>The 17th century saw the birth of the <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French colonial empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch Empire</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/English_overseas_possessions" title="English overseas possessions">English overseas possessions</a>, which later became the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. It also saw the establishment of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danish_colonial_empire" title="Danish colonial empire">Danish colonial empire</a> and some <a href="/wiki/Swedish_overseas_colonies" title="Swedish overseas colonies">Swedish overseas colonies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>A first wave of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independence_movement" title="Independence movement">independence movements</a> started with the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a> (1775–1783), initiating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_British_Empire" title="Second British Empire">a new phase for the British Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The Spanish Empire largely collapsed in the Americas with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_American_wars_of_independence" title="Latin American wars of independence">Latin American wars of independence</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">  1808</span> onwards). Empire-builders established several new colonies after this time, including in the <a href="/wiki/German_colonial_empire" title="German colonial empire">German colonial empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_colonial_empire" title="Belgian colonial empire">Belgian colonial empire</a>. In the late-19th century, many European powers became involved in the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_monarchy" title="Habsburg monarchy">Austrian Empire</a> existed at the same time as the above empires but did not expand over oceans. Rather, these empires expanded through the more traditional route of the conquest of neighbouring territories. There was, though, some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_colonisation_of_the_Americas" title="Russian colonisation of the Americas">Russian colonisation of the Americas</a> across the Bering Strait. From the 1860s, the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> modelled itself on European colonial empires and expanded its territories in the Pacific and on the Asian mainland. <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a> fought for hegemony in South America.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="colonialism? (February 2021)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_of_America" title="United States of America">United States of America</a> gained overseas territories after the 1898 <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a> – hence the coining of the term <a href="/wiki/American_imperialism" title="American imperialism">"American Empire"</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1432" data-file-width="1815" decoding="async" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg/330px-Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg/495px-Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg/660px-Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> (as of 1910)</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_Governor_inspection_1972.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="943" data-file-width="908" decoding="async" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Seychelles_Governor_inspection_1972.jpg/220px-Seychelles_Governor_inspection_1972.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Seychelles_Governor_inspection_1972.jpg/330px-Seychelles_Governor_inspection_1972.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Seychelles_Governor_inspection_1972.jpg/440px-Seychelles_Governor_inspection_1972.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_Governor_inspection_1972.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Colonial Governor of the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> inspecting police guard of honour in 1972</div></div></div>
<p>The world's colonial population at the outbreak of the First World War (1914) – a high point for colonialism – totalled about 560 million people, of whom 70% lived in British possessions, 10% in French possessions, 9% in Dutch possessions, 4% in Japanese possessions, 2% in German possessions, 2% in American possessions, 3% in Portuguese possessions, 1% in Belgian possessions and 0.5% in Italian possessions. The domestic domains of the colonial powers had a total population of about 370 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Outside Europe, few areas had remained without coming under formal colonial tutorship – and even <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siam" title="Siam">Siam</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Empire" title="Chinese Empire">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">Persia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Empire" title="Ethiopian Empire">Abyssinia</a> had felt varying degrees of Western colonial-style influence – <a href="/wiki/Concessions_and_leases_in_international_relations" title="Concessions and leases in international relations">concessions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unequal_treaty" title="Unequal treaty">unequal treaties</a>, <a href="/wiki/Extraterritoriality" title="Extraterritoriality">extraterritoriality</a> and the like.
</p><p>Asking whether colonies paid, economic historian <a href="/wiki/Grover_Clark" title="Grover Clark">Grover Clark</a> (1891–1938) argues an emphatic "No!" He reports that in every case the support cost, especially the military system necessary to support and defend colonies, outran the total trade they produced. Apart from the British Empire, they did not provide favoured destinations for the immigration of surplus metropole populations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The question of whether colonies paid is a complicated one when recognizing the multiplicity of interests involved. In some cases colonial powers paid a lot in military costs while private investors pocketed the benefits. In other cases the colonial powers managed to move the burden of administrative costs to the colonies themselves by imposing taxes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a> of 1914–1918, the victorious <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">allies</a> divided up the German colonial empire and much of the Ottoman Empire between themselves as <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandates</a>, grouping these territories into three classes according to how quickly it was deemed that they could prepare for independence. The empires of Russia and Austria collapsed in 1917–1918.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> set up short-lived colonial systems (<i><a href="/wiki/Reichskommissariat" title="Reichskommissariat">Reichskommissariate</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/General_Government" title="General Government"><i>Generalgouvernement</i></a>) in Eastern Europe in the early 1940s.
</p><p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> (1939–1945) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decolonisation" title="Decolonisation">decolonisation</a> progressed rapidly, due to a number of reasons. First, the Japanese victories in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">Pacific War</a> of 1941–1945 had showed <a href="/wiki/Indian_people" title="Indian people">Indians</a> and other subject peoples that the colonial powers were not invincible. Second, World War II had significantly weakened all the overseas colonial powers economically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (February 2021)">need quotation to verify</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The word "<a href="/wiki/Neocolonialism" title="Neocolonialism">neocolonialism</a>" originated from <a href="/wiki/Jean-Paul_Sartre" title="Jean-Paul Sartre">Jean-Paul Sartre</a> in 1956,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> to refer to a variety of contexts since the decolonisation that took place after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. Generally it does not refer to a type of direct colonisation – rather to colonialism or colonial-style exploitation by other means. Specifically, neocolonialism may refer to the theory that former or existing economic relationships, such as the <a href="/wiki/General_Agreement_on_Tariffs_and_Trade" title="General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade">General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Central American Free Trade Agreement">Central American Free Trade Agreement</a>, or the operations of companies (such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>) fostered by former colonial powers were or are used to maintain control of former colonies and dependencies after the colonial independence movements of the post–World War II period.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The term "neocolonialism" became popular in ex-colonies in the late-20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_colonies">List of colonies</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British">British</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hakewill,_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica,_Plate_04.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1663" data-file-width="2505" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Hakewill%2C_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica%2C_Plate_04.jpg/220px-Hakewill%2C_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica%2C_Plate_04.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Hakewill%2C_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica%2C_Plate_04.jpg/330px-Hakewill%2C_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica%2C_Plate_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Hakewill%2C_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica%2C_Plate_04.jpg/440px-Hakewill%2C_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica%2C_Plate_04.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hakewill,_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica,_Plate_04.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Harbour Street, <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Jamaica" title="Kingston, Jamaica">Kingston, Jamaica</a>, c. 1820</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Isandhlwana.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="588" data-file-width="944" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Isandhlwana.jpg/220px-Isandhlwana.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Isandhlwana.jpg/330px-Isandhlwana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Isandhlwana.jpg/440px-Isandhlwana.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Isandhlwana.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Isandlwana" title="Battle of Isandlwana">Battle of Isandlwana</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Zulu_War" title="Anglo-Zulu War">Anglo-Zulu War</a> of 1879. After an initial defeat the British were able to conquer <a href="/wiki/Zulu_Kingdom" title="Zulu Kingdom">Zululand</a>.</div></div></div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mestizo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="475" data-file-width="698" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Mestizo.jpg/220px-Mestizo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Mestizo.jpg/330px-Mestizo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Mestizo.jpg/440px-Mestizo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mestizo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An 18th-century <a href="/wiki/Casta" title="Casta">casta</a> painting from <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a> shows a Spanish man and his indigenous wife.</div></div></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Omani">Omani</span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Analysis_of_Western_European_colonialism_and_colonization#Colonial_actions_and_their_impacts" title="Analysis of Western European colonialism and colonization">Analysis of Western European colonialism and colonization § Colonial actions and their impacts</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Satterfield_cartoon_about_brutalities_committed_by_Western_nations.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2294" data-file-width="1864" decoding="async" height="271" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Satterfield_cartoon_about_brutalities_committed_by_Western_nations.jpg/220px-Satterfield_cartoon_about_brutalities_committed_by_Western_nations.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Satterfield_cartoon_about_brutalities_committed_by_Western_nations.jpg/330px-Satterfield_cartoon_about_brutalities_committed_by_Western_nations.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Satterfield_cartoon_about_brutalities_committed_by_Western_nations.jpg/440px-Satterfield_cartoon_about_brutalities_committed_by_Western_nations.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Satterfield_cartoon_about_brutalities_committed_by_Western_nations.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 1904 cartoon by <a href="/wiki/Bob_Satterfield_(cartoonist)" title="Bob Satterfield (cartoonist)">Bob Satterfield</a> about the brutality committed by Western nations: the personifications of England, the United States, and Germany carrying spears topped by the severed heads of Tibet, the Philippines, and Southwest Africa respectively. The caption describes this as "The advance guard of civilization".</div></div></div>

<p>The impacts of colonisation are immense and pervasive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Various effects, both immediate and protracted, include the spread of virulent <a href="/wiki/Pandemic" title="Pandemic">diseases</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oppression" title="Oppression">unequal social relations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detribalization" title="Detribalization">detribalization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exploitation_of_natural_resources" title="Exploitation of natural resources">exploitation</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enslavement" title="Enslavement">enslavement</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_medicine#Modern_medicine" title="History of medicine">medical advances</a>, the creation of new institutions, <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Africa#Abolition" title="Slavery in Africa">abolitionism</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lovejoy,_Paul_E._2012_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lovejoy,_Paul_E._2012-49">[49]</a></sup> improved infrastructure,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> and technological progress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Colonial practices also spur the spread of colonist languages, literature and cultural institutions, while endangering or obliterating those of native peoples. The native cultures of the colonised peoples can also have a powerful influence on the imperial country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Economy.2C_trade_and_commerce"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy,_trade_and_commerce">Economy, trade and commerce</span></h3>
<p>Economic expansion, sometimes described as the <a href="/wiki/Colonial_surplus" title="Colonial surplus">colonial surplus</a>, has accompanied imperial expansion since ancient times.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Greek trade networks spread throughout the Mediterranean region while Roman trade expanded with the primary goal of directing tribute from the colonised areas towards the Roman metropole. According to <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a>, by the time of emperor <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a>, up to 120 Roman ships would set sail every year from <a href="/wiki/Myos_Hormos" title="Myos Hormos">Myos Hormos</a> in <a href="/wiki/Roman_Egypt" title="Roman Egypt">Roman Egypt</a> to India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> With the development of trade routes under the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>,
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gujari" title="Gujari">Gujari</a> Hindus, Syrian Muslims, Jews, Armenians, Christians from south and central Europe operated trading routes that supplied Persian and Arab horses to the armies of all three empires, Mocha coffee to <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>, Persian silk to India and <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1188" data-file-width="2835" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png/330px-16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png/495px-16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png/660px-16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:16th_century_Portuguese_Spanish_trade_routes.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese trade routes</a> (blue) and the rival <a href="/wiki/Manila_galleon" title="Manila galleon">Manila-Acapulco galleons</a> trade routes (white) established in 1568</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aztec_civilisation" title="Aztec civilisation">Aztec civilisation</a> developed into an extensive empire that, much like the Roman Empire, had the goal of exacting tribute from the conquered colonial areas. For the Aztecs, a significant tribute was the acquisition of sacrificial victims for their religious rituals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>On the other hand, European colonial empires sometimes attempted to channel, restrict and impede trade involving their colonies, funneling activity through the metropole and taxing accordingly.
</p><p>Despite the general trend of economic expansion, the economic performance of former European colonies varies significantly. In "Institutions as a Fundamental Cause of Long-run Growth", economists <a href="/wiki/Daron_Acemoglu" title="Daron Acemoglu">Daron Acemoglu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Johnson_(economist)" title="Simon Johnson (economist)">Simon Johnson</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_A._Robinson_(Harvard_University)" title="James A. Robinson (Harvard University)">James A. Robinson</a> compare the economic influences of the European colonists on different colonies and study what could explain the huge discrepancies in previous European colonies, for example, between West African colonies like <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Institutions_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Institutions-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the paper, economic institutions are the determinant of the colonial success because they determine their financial performance and order for the distribution of resources. At the same time, these institutions are also consequences of political institutions – especially how <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a> and <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a> political power is allocated. To explain the different colonial cases, we thus need to look first into the political institutions that shaped the economic institutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Institutions_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-Institutions-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_Castro,_Lorenzo_-_A_Dutch_East-Indiaman_off_Hoorn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2098" data-file-width="2501" decoding="async" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/A_Castro%2C_Lorenzo_-_A_Dutch_East-Indiaman_off_Hoorn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/220px-A_Castro%2C_Lorenzo_-_A_Dutch_East-Indiaman_off_Hoorn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/A_Castro%2C_Lorenzo_-_A_Dutch_East-Indiaman_off_Hoorn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/330px-A_Castro%2C_Lorenzo_-_A_Dutch_East-Indiaman_off_Hoorn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/A_Castro%2C_Lorenzo_-_A_Dutch_East-Indiaman_off_Hoorn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/440px-A_Castro%2C_Lorenzo_-_A_Dutch_East-Indiaman_off_Hoorn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_Castro,_Lorenzo_-_A_Dutch_East-Indiaman_off_Hoorn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> was the first-ever <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporation</a>, financed by shares that established the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">first modern stock exchange</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>For example, one interesting observation is "the Reversal of Fortune" – the less developed civilisations in 1500, like North America, Australia, and New Zealand, are now much richer than those countries who used to be in the prosperous civilisations in 1500 before the colonists came, like the Mughals in India and the Incas in the Americas. One explanation offered by the paper focuses on the political institutions of the various colonies: it was less likely for European colonists to introduce economic institutions where they could benefit quickly from the extraction of resources in the area. Therefore, given a more developed civilisation and denser population, European colonists would rather keep the existing economic systems than introduce an entirely new system; while in places with little to extract, European colonists would rather establish new economic institutions to protect their interests. Political institutions thus gave rise to different types of economic systems, which determined the colonial economic performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Institutions_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-Institutions-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>European colonisation and development also changed gendered systems of power already in place around the world. In many pre-colonialist areas, women maintained power, prestige, or authority through reproductive or agricultural control. For example, in certain parts of sub-Saharan Africa<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(geographic_names)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (geographic names)"><span title="The geographic scope near this tag is ambiguous. (May 2021)">where?</span></a></i>]</sup>      women maintained farmland in which they had usage rights. While men would make political and communal decisions for a community, the women would control the village's food supply or their individual family's land. This allowed women to achieve power and autonomy, even in patrilineal and patriarchal societies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p><p>Through the rise of European colonialism came a large push for development and industrialisation of most economic systems. When working to improve productivity, Europeans focused mostly on male workers. Foreign aid arrived in the form of loans, land, credit, and tools to speed up development, but were only allocated to men. In a more European fashion, women were expected to serve on a more domestic level. The result was a technologic, economic, and class-based gender gap that widened over time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>Within a colony, the presence of extractive colonial institutions in a given area has been found have effects on the modern day economic development, institutions and infrastructure of these areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Slavery_and_indentured_servitude">Slavery and indentured servitude</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indentured_servant" title="Indentured servant">Indentured servant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coolie" title="Coolie">Coolie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Blackbirding" title="Blackbirding">Blackbirding</a></div>
<p>European nations entered their imperial projects with the goal of enriching the European metropoles. Exploitation of non-Europeans and of other Europeans to support imperial goals was acceptable to the colonisers. Two outgrowths of this imperial agenda were the extension of slavery and indentured servitude. In the 17th century, nearly two-thirds of English settlers came to North America as indentured servants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>European slave traders brought large numbers of African slaves to the Americas by sail. Spain and Portugal had <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">brought African slaves</a> to work in African colonies such as <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="São Tomé and Príncipe">São Tomé and Príncipe</a>, and then in Latin America, by the 16th century. The British, French and Dutch joined in the slave trade in subsequent centuries. The European colonial system took approximately 11 million Africans to the Caribbean and to North and South America as slaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-King_2010_24_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-King_2010_24-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3585" data-file-width="2531" decoding="async" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg/170px-Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg/255px-Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg/340px-Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Slave traders in Gorée, <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a>, 18th century</div></div></div>
